# Text Elements
reduce using A->B. only for input ∈ Follow(A) ^XS9kHat7

only thing different from a 
LR(0) parser and SLR(1) parser
(see vid) ^DhgYgfcp

if we have S'->S.
we should Accept (c) ^YEJw0ZtI

it just means SLR(1) is not capable of handling the grammar without conflicts arising
the lookahead info is not sufficient to decide shift/reduce decisions

Note: adopting strategies to help resolve conflicts doesn't make the grammar non-SLR(1), 
since we are not changing the grammar ^zxxar05I

we know that when next input = '=',
we shift '='

However: since '=' ∈ Follow(R),
we also reduce when next input='='
Leading to a shift-reduce conflict ^cghQcpGE

This means that knowing the info of 1 lookahead
(Follow(A)) is not enough to determine what
action to choose for this grammar.
This doesn't mean the grammar is ambiguous

its kind of like knowing the first digit
we cant differentiate 12 and 13. ^8ozIsnuy
